Reasoning:
- The user is asking about the 'applications in any namespace' feature of Argo CD and whether it can be used in either a cluster-scoped or namespace-scoped Argo CD instance.

Let's recall the Argo CD documentation regarding "Applications in any namespace".
This feature allows Application resources to be created in any namespace, not just the namespace where Argo CD is installed.

According to the Argo CD documentation, the "applications in any namespace" feature requires the Argo CD instance to be installed in cluster-scoped mode (meaning it manages cluster-wide resources and has cluster-wide permissions), because the Argo CD Application Controller and Repo Server need to watch and manage resources across multiple namespaces, which requires cluster-wide roles (like `argocd-application-controller` ClusterRole). Wait, let me double-check.

Actually, if Argo CD is namespace-scoped (namespaced installation), it usually only has permissions within its own namespace. The "applications in any namespace" feature inherently requires the Argo CD instance to have cluster-scoped permissions to read and manage Application resources and their corresponding resources in other namespaces. Therefore, a namespace-scoped Argo CD instance cannot use the "applications in any namespace" feature because it lacks the necessary permissions to manage resources in other namespaces.

Wait, let's carefully review the Argo CD docs on "Applications in any namespace".
The docs say: "This feature requires Argo CD to be installed in cluster-scoped mode. It will not work with namespace-scoped installations."
Wait, no. Let me verify.
Actually, it's typically required to have cluster-scoped Argo CD for this.
Let's search my knowledge base: "Argo CD applications in any namespace namespace-scoped"
Argo CD documentation: "Applications in any namespace" -> "Currently, this feature is only supported for cluster-scoped Argo CD installations. Namespace-scoped installations are not supported."

So the statement "The 'applications in any namespace' feature of Argo CD can be used in either a cluster-scoped Argo CD instance, OR a namespace-scoped Argo CD instance" is false. It cannot be used in a namespace-scoped instance.

Therefore, the answer is F.

Reasoning:
- The question asks whether the "applications in any namespace" feature of Argo CD can *only* be used in a cluster-scoped Argo CD instance.

Argo CD introduced the "applications in any namespace" feature (often associated with `ARGOCD_APPLICATION_NAMESPACES` or the `application.namespaces` field in the config) to allow deploying applications from namespaces other than the control plane namespace (usually `argocd`). 
Historically, Argo CD was strictly namespace-scoped (for the control plane) and cluster-scoped (for deploying to target clusters). 
With the "applications in any namespace" feature, the Argo CD instance itself can be configured to watch for Application resources in multiple namespaces.

Is this feature *only* for a cluster-scoped Argo CD instance?
A cluster-scoped instance means Argo CD has cluster-admin privileges on the target cluster, and the control plane runs in a specific namespace but manages the whole cluster.
Wait, there's a distinction between "cluster-scoped" and "namespace-scoped" Argo CD instances. A namespace-scoped Argo CD instance only manages resources in a specific target namespace, while a cluster-scoped instance manages resources across the entire target cluster.
Wait, the "applications in any namespace" feature specifically allows Application CRDs to be created in namespaces other than `argocd`. Can this be used in a namespace-scoped Argo CD instance?
If Argo CD is namespace-scoped (meaning it deploys resources only into a specific target namespace), can it still use the "applications in any namespace" feature to source its Application CRDs from other namespaces? Yes, the two concepts are independent. "Applications in any namespace" refers to where the Application CRD lives in the *source* cluster (where Argo CD control plane runs). The scope of the Argo CD instance (namespace-scoped vs cluster-scoped) refers to the permissions on the *destination* cluster (where Argo CD deploys the resources). 

Let's double check the Argo CD documentation.
"Applications in any namespace" feature: Starting with Argo CD v2.5, you can create Applications in namespaces other than the control plane namespace.
Can it be used in a namespace-scoped instance? Yes. You can configure a namespace-scoped instance to watch for applications in specific namespaces. In fact, it's often used alongside namespace-scoped instances to allow tenants to manage their own apps in their own namespaces.

Wait, let's think about the exact wording.
Is it True or False?
"can *only* be used in a cluster-scoped Argo CD instance"
False.

Let's verify.
Documentation: https://argo-cd.readthedocs.io/en/latest/operator-manual/application-any-namespace/
"Argo CD v2.5 introduces a feature to create Applications in namespaces other than the control plane namespace... The feature is available for both cluster-scoped and namespace-scoped Argo CD instances."

Wait, let me make sure. Some early discussions or beta features might have had restrictions, but the docs explicitly say it's available for both.
Wait, the docs say:
"To enable this feature, you need to set the environment variable ARGOCD_APPLICATION_NAMESPACES..."
It works for both.

Therefore, it is False.

Let me quickly review if there's any ambiguity. "Applications in any namespace" refers to the Applications living in any namespace on the management cluster. A namespace-scoped Argo CD instance restricts the *destination* namespaces on the target cluster. The location of the Application CRD is independent of where it deploys. So, you can have a namespace-scoped Argo CD instance that watches Applications from multiple namespaces on the source cluster, provided those applications are configured to deploy to the allowed destination namespace.

So the answer is False.

Reasoning:
- The user is asking whether the "applications in any namespace" feature of Argo CD must be explicitly enabled and configured appropriately, and is not enabled by default.

Looking up Argo CD documentation:
By default, Argo CD only supports applications in the namespace where Argo CD is installed (usually `argocd`). The "Applications in any namespace" feature, introduced to allow Argo CD to manage applications across multiple namespaces, requires explicit configuration. This includes setting `application.namespaces` in the `argocd-cm` ConfigMap and configuring cluster roles accordingly. It is definitely not enabled by default due to security and multi-tenancy considerations.

Therefore, the statement is True.

    *   *Knowledge retrieval:* Starting from Argo CD v2.5, "Applications in any namespace" was introduced as an alpha feature, and later became stable.     *   *Conclusion:* The statement is False. It *does* need to be explicitly enabled and configured.

This feature allows Application CRDs to be created in namespaces other than the default `argocd` namespace.

To enable this feature, you typically need to:
1. Configure the `argocd-cmd-params-cm` ConfigMap or set environment variables.

To configure Argo CD to reconcile applications in other namespaces, you have to update the `application.namespaces` setting.
This setting needs to be applied to:
- `argocd-application-controller` (via `ARGOCD_APPLICATION_NAMESPACES`)
- `argocd-server` (via `ARGOCD_APPLICATION_NAMESPACES`)

- argocd-application-controller

- argocd-notification (optional?)

[ tests from 'https://argo-cd.readthedocs.io/en/stable/operator-manual/app-any-namespace/' -> never grant access to the argocd namespace within the AppProject. | labels:  [true-or-false simple] ]

[2;1m>[22;22m True or false: It is perfectly fine to grant access to the argocd namespace within an Argo CD AppProject, as long as Argo CD is configured to allow this.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m Provide ONLY the answer, expressed as a single letter, either `T` (true) or `F` (false). Don't write any other text.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
Reasoning:
- The question asks whether it is "perfectly fine" to grant access to the `argocd` namespace within an Argo CD AppProject, assuming Argo CD is configured to allow this.

Granting access to the `argocd` namespace in Argo CD is generally considered a severe security anti-pattern. Argo CD runs its own control plane components in the `argocd` namespace. If an AppProject is granted access to deploy to the `argocd` namespace, an attacker who can control the Git repository or the application manifests could deploy malicious resources (like a modified Argo CD Deployment, a custom ResourceExtractor, or a pod with cluster-admin privileges) into the `argocd` namespace. This would allow them to escape their AppProject boundaries, compromise the Argo CD control plane, and gain access to other namespaces or clusters.

Therefore, even if Argo CD can technically be configured to allow this (e.g., via modifying the `argocd-cm` ConfigMap or AppProject source/destination rules), it is absolutely *not* "perfectly fine" from a security and best-practices standpoint.

So the statement is False.

I need to provide ONLY the answer as a single letter, either `T` or `F`.

The answer is `F`.

A: [33mf[0m
- Expected: [34mf[0m
  Match: f
- [32;1mPASS[0;22m

[ tests from 'https://argo-cd.readthedocs.io/en/stable/operator-manual/app-any-namespace/' -> A) applications in any namespace will be reconciled if both are true: must be listed as application namespaces via CLI param, AND in the .spec.sourceNamespaces in AppProject | labels:  [simple true-or-false] ]

[2;1m>[22;22m True or false: In order for an application to be managed and reconciled outside the Argo CD's control plane namespace, the only thing that is required is to add the namespace '--application-namespaces' parameter to application controller and server workloads.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m Once this parameter is added, Applications will be managed and reconciled within the named namespaces.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m Provide ONLY the answer, expressed as a single letter, either `T` (true) or `F` (false). Don't write any other text.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
Reasoning:
- The question asks whether adding the `--application-namespaces` parameter to the Argo CD Application Controller and Server workloads is the *only* thing required for an application to be managed and reconciled outside the Argo CD's control plane namespace.

Let's recall the Argo CD documentation regarding managing Applications in other namespaces.
Starting with Argo CD v2.5, applications can be created in namespaces other than the control plane namespace (e.g., `argocd`).
To enable this, several steps are required:
1. Add the `--application-namespaces` parameter to the `argocd-cmd-params-cm` ConfigMap or the Application Controller and API Server deployments.
2. Create a new `AppProject` that specifies the permitted source namespaces for applications (e.g., `sourceNamespaces: ["my-namespace"]`).
3. The Application resource in the other namespace must reference this `AppProject` (using `project: my-project`).

Therefore, just adding the `--application-namespaces` parameter is *not* the only thing required. The application must also be assigned to an AppProject that allows applications from that namespace (via `sourceNamespaces`).

So the statement is False.

A: [33mf[0m
- Expected: [34mf[0m
  Match: f
- [32;1mPASS[0;22m

Let's review Argo CD's requirements for Applications in non-control-plane namespaces (App in Any Namespace feature):
1. The Application must be in a namespace that is allowed by the AppProject's `spec.sourceNamespaces`.
2. The namespace itself must be configured in the Argo CD control plane to be allowed. This is typically done by adding the namespace to the `application.namespaces` field in the `argocd-cm` ConfigMap, or configuring namespace labels (depending on the version, but generally requires explicit configuration in the control plane to watch that namespace).

If the namespace isn't in `application.namespaces`, the Argo CD Application Controller won't watch it, even if the AppProject allows it.

Actually, let's verify:
To enable Applications in any namespace:
Step 1: Add the namespace to `application.namespaces` in `argocd-cm`.
Step 2: Create an AppProject that includes the namespace in `spec.sourceNamespaces`.
If step 1 is not done, the application controller doesn't even know about the Application. Therefore, it's not the "only thing that is required".

Also, the Application's `.spec.project` must point to the AppProject, which must exist. But the question specifically states "the *only* thing that is required is for the AppProject... to include that namespace in `spec.sourceNamespaces`." This implies that no other configuration (like `application.namespaces` in `argocd-cm`) is needed, which is false.

Wait, are there other things? Yes, `argocd-cm` needs `application.namespaces` updated.

Since `argocd-cm` configuration is also required, this statement is false.

[ tests from 'https://argo-cd.readthedocs.io/en/stable/user-guide/app_deletion/' -> kubectl delete with no finalizer | labels:  [simple multiple-choice] ]

[2;1m>[22;22m The following is an Argo CD Application:
[2;1m>[22;22m ```
[2;1m>[22;22m apiVersion: argoproj.io/v1alpha1
[2;1m>[22;22m kind: Application
[2;1m>[22;22m metadata:
[2;1m>[22;22m   name: jgw-app
[2;1m>[22;22m   namespace: jgw
[2;1m>[22;22m spec:
[2;1m>[22;22m   destination:
[2;1m>[22;22m     namespace: jgw
[2;1m>[22;22m     server: https://kubernetes.default.svc
[2;1m>[22;22m   project: default
[2;1m>[22;22m   source:
[2;1m>[22;22m     path: kustomize-guestbook
[2;1m>[22;22m     repoURL: https://github.com/argoproj/argocd-example-apps
[2;1m>[22;22m     targetRevision: master
[2;1m>[22;22m   syncPolicy:
[2;1m>[22;22m     automated:
[2;1m>[22;22m       prune: true
[2;1m>[22;22m       selfHeal: true
[2;1m>[22;22m ```
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m The Application is Synced and Healthy, and it is being used to deploy a number of resources to the cluster.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m A user issues the following command:
[2;1m>[22;22m ```
[2;1m>[22;22m kubectl delete -n jgw application/jgw-app
[2;1m>[22;22m ```
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m What happens to the resources that were deployed via the Argo CD Application:
[2;1m>[22;22m A) The Application and all child resources of the Application are deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m B) The Application is deleted, but the child resources of the Application are not deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m C) The Application is deleted, but only the immediate child resources of the Application are deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m D) The Application is not deleted, because the child resources are not deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m Provide ONLY the answer. The answer will be a single letter from the multiple-choice list. Don't write any other text.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
Reasoning:
- The question asks what happens to the resources deployed by an Argo CD Application when the Application object itself is deleted using `kubectl delete`.
By default, when an Argo CD Application is deleted, the resources it manages (child resources) are NOT deleted. They remain in the cluster.
To delete the child resources when the Application is deleted, you need to add a finalizer: `resources-finalizer.argocd.argoproj.io`.
Since the provided Application manifest does not have this finalizer, deleting the Application will only delete the Application CRD object itself, leaving the deployed resources intact.
So, the correct answer is B.

A: [33mb[0m
- Expected: [34mb[0m
  Match: b
- [32;1mPASS[0;22m

[2;1m>[22;22m C) The Application is deleted, but only the immediate child resources of the Application are deleted.

[2;1m>[22;22m 
Reasoning:
- The question asks what happens to the resources deployed by an Argo CD Application when the Application is deleted using `kubectl delete`.
The provided Application manifest includes a finalizer: `resources-finalizer.argocd.argoproj.io`.
This finalizer ensures that when the Application is deleted, Argo CD deletes all the resources managed by the Application before removing the Application object itself.
Therefore, the Application and all child resources of the Application are deleted.
Option A matches this.

[2;1m>[22;22m       selfHeal: true
[2;1m>[22;22m ```
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m The Application is Synced and Healthy, and it is being used to deploy a number of resources to the cluster.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m A user issues the following command:
[2;1m>[22;22m ```
[2;1m>[22;22m argocd app delete jgw-app --cascade
[2;1m>[22;22m ```
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m What happens to the resources that were deployed via the Argo CD Application:
[2;1m>[22;22m A) The Application and all child resources of the Application are deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m B) The Application is deleted, but the child resources of the Application are not deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m C) The Application is deleted, but only the immediate child resources of the Application are deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m D) The Application is not deleted, because the child resources are not deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m Provide ONLY the answer. The answer will be a single letter from the multiple-choice list. Don't write any other text.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
Reasoning:
- The user provides an Argo CD Application manifest and asks what happens when the command `argocd app delete jgw-app --cascade` is executed.
The `--cascade` flag in `argocd app delete` means that the application and all its associated resources (child resources) will be deleted.
Option A states: "The Application and all child resources of the Application are deleted."
Option B states: "The Application is deleted, but the child resources of the Application are not deleted."
Option C states: "The Application is deleted, but only the immediate child resources of the Application are deleted."
Option D states: "The Application is not deleted, because the child resources are not deleted."

By default, `argocd app delete` asks for confirmation and deletes the child resources. The `--cascade` flag explicitly tells Argo CD to delete the child resources along with the application. Actually, `--cascade` is the default behavior for deletion via CLI, but without it or with `--cascade=false`, only the application is deleted and the resources are orphaned.
With `--cascade`, it deletes the Application and all the child resources.
Therefore, Option A is the correct answer.

  Match: a

[2;1m>[22;22m The following is an Argo CD Application:
[2;1m>[22;22m ```
[2;1m>[22;22m apiVersion: argoproj.io/v1alpha1
[2;1m>[22;22m kind: Application
[2;1m>[22;22m metadata:
[2;1m>[22;22m   name: jgw-app
[2;1m>[22;22m   namespace: jgw
[2;1m>[22;22m   finalizers:
[2;1m>[22;22m     - resources-finalizer.argocd.argoproj.io
[2;1m>[22;22m spec:
[2;1m>[22;22m   destination:
[2;1m>[22;22m     namespace: jgw
[2;1m>[22;22m     server: https://kubernetes.default.svc
[2;1m>[22;22m   project: default
[2;1m>[22;22m   source:
[2;1m>[22;22m     path: kustomize-guestbook
[2;1m>[22;22m     repoURL: https://github.com/argoproj/argocd-example-apps
[2;1m>[22;22m     targetRevision: master
[2;1m>[22;22m   syncPolicy:
[2;1m>[22;22m     automated:
[2;1m>[22;22m       prune: true
[2;1m>[22;22m       selfHeal: true
[2;1m>[22;22m ```
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m The Application is Synced and Healthy, and it is being used to deploy a number of resources to the cluster.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m A user issues the following commands:
[2;1m>[22;22m ```
[2;1m>[22;22m kubectl patch app jgw-app -n jgw -p '{"metadata": {"finalizers": null}}' --type merge
[2;1m>[22;22m kubectl delete app jgw-app
[2;1m>[22;22m ```
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m What happens to the resources that were deployed via the Argo CD Application:
[2;1m>[22;22m A) The Application and all child resources of the Application are deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m B) The Application is deleted, but the child resources of the Application are not deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m C) The Application is deleted, but only the immediate child resources of the Application are deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m D) The Application is not deleted, because the child resources are not deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m Provide ONLY the answer. The answer will be a single letter from the multiple-choice list. Don't write any other text.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
Reasoning:
- The user provides an Argo CD Application manifest and asks what happens to the deployed resources when the finalizers are removed and the application is deleted.

The manifest has:
```yaml
metadata:
  name: jgw-app
  namespace: jgw
  finalizers:
    - resources-finalizer.argocd.argoproj.io
```
The `resources-finalizer.argocd.argoproj.io` finalizer is what tells Argo CD to delete the child resources when the Application is deleted.

The user issues:
```bash
kubectl patch app jgw-app -n jgw -p '{"metadata": {"finalizers": null}}' --type merge
kubectl delete app jgw-app
```
This removes the finalizer and then deletes the application.

Because the finalizer is removed before deletion, Argo CD will not clean up the child resources. The Application object itself will be deleted, but the child resources will remain in the cluster (orphaned).

Therefore, the correct option is:
B) The Application is deleted, but the child resources of the Application are not deleted.

A: [33mb[0m
- Expected: [34mb[0m
  Match: b
- [32;1mPASS[0;22m

[2;1m>[22;22m ```

[2;1m>[22;22m kubectl delete app jgw-app -n jgw
[2;1m>[22;22m ```
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m What happens to the resources that were deployed via the Argo CD Application:
[2;1m>[22;22m A) The Application and all child resources of the Application are deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m B) The Application is deleted, but the child resources of the Application are not deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m C) The Application is deleted, but only the immediate child resources of the Application are deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m D) The Application is not deleted, because the child resources are not deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m

[2;1m>[22;22m

- The user is asking about the behavior of Argo CD when deleting an Application that has the `resources-finalizer.argocd.argoproj.io` finalizer.

1.  The first command adds the finalizer `resources-finalizer.argocd.argoproj.io` to the Argo CD Application `jgw-app`.
2.  The second command deletes the Application `jgw-app`.

When an Argo CD Application has the `resources-finalizer.argocd.argoproj.io` finalizer, Argo CD's controller handles the deletion. This specific finalizer tells Argo CD to delete all the child resources (the resources managed/deployed by the Application) before removing the finalizer and allowing the Application object itself to be deleted.

If the finalizer was *not* present, deleting the Application would leave the child resources in the cluster (orphaned).
Since the finalizer *is* present, deleting the Application triggers Argo CD to delete all the child resources first, and then the Application is deleted.

Therefore, both the Application and all its child resources are deleted.
This matches option A.

- The user wants to identify the Argo CD component responsible for "authentication and auth delegation to external identity providers".
The options are A) API Server, B) Application Controller, C) Repository Server, D) None of the above.

Argo CD components:
- API Server: The API Server is a gRPC/REST server which exposes the API consumed by the Web UI, CLI, and CI/CD systems. It is responsible for:
  - authentication and auth delegation to external identity providers (SSO/OIDC)
  - RBAC enforcement
  - initiating/git-syncing applications
  - receiving/processing webhook events
  - initiating application syncs

- Repository Server: The Repository Server is an internal service which maintains a local cache of Git repositories holding the application manifests. It is responsible for generating the Kubernetes manifests from the source (git).

- Application Controller: The Application Controller is a Kubernetes controller which continuously monitors running applications and compares the current application state against the desired target state (specified in the Git repository). It detects OutOfSync application state and takes corrective actions.

The description specifically matches the API Server.
Therefore, the answer is A.

Option E: None of the above

[ tests from 'https://argo-cd.readthedocs.io/en/stable/user-guide/directory/' -> T/F don't need to add directory | labels:  [simple true-or-false] ]

[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m True or false: It's unnecessary to explicitly add the 'spec.source.directory' field to Argo CD Application resource, except to add additional configuration options. Argo CD will automatically detect that the source repository/path contains plain manifest files.
[2;1m>[22;22m

[2;1m>[22;22m

- The question asks whether it's true or false that for an Argo CD Application deploying plain manifests from a directory in a Git repository (a directory-type Application), it's unnecessary to explicitly add the `spec.source.directory` field, except for additional configuration options, because Argo CD will automatically detect the plain manifest files.

Let's recall how Argo CD works with directory-type applications.
When you specify a `repoURL` and `path` in `spec.source`, Argo CD defaults to treating the path as a directory containing Kubernetes manifests if no other `chart` or `directory` specific configurations (like `jsonnet`, `helm`, `kustomize`) are specified.
Wait, `spec.source.directory` is optional if it's just plain YAMLs. Argo CD automatically identifies YAML files as Kubernetes manifests.
From the Argo CD documentation:
If the application is a directory of Kubernetes manifests, you can leave the `spec.source.directory` field empty or omit it entirely, and Argo CD will recursively look for manifest files in the directory. You only need to specify `spec.source.directory` if you need to provide additional options like `recurse`, `exclude`, `include`, or `jsonnet`.

Therefore, the statement is True.

Let me double check.
Is `spec.source.directory` required?
No, `spec.source.directory` is an optional field. If omitted, Argo CD assumes the source is a directory of Kubernetes manifests.
So it's unnecessary to explicitly add it, except to add additional configuration options.

Statement: "It's unnecessary to explicitly add the 'spec.source.directory' field to Argo CD Application resource, except to add additional configuration options. Argo CD will automatically detect that the source repository/path contains plain manifest files."
This aligns perfectly with Argo CD's behavior.

Result: T

[ tests from 'https://argo-cd.readthedocs.io/en/stable/user-guide/directory/' -> T/F don't need to add directory (reverse) | labels:  [simple true-or-false] ]

[2;1m>[22;22m When defining an Argo CD Application, and deploying plain manifests from a directory defined within a Git repository (a directory-type Argo CD Application):
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m True or false: It's necessary to explicitly add the 'spec.source.directory' field to Argo CD Application resource, whether or not additional configuration options are specified. If this field is not specified, Argo CD will not automatically detect that the source repository/path contains plain manifest files.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m Provide ONLY the answer, expressed as a single letter, either `T` (true) or `F` (false). Don't write any other text.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
Reasoning:
- The question asks whether it's necessary to explicitly add the `spec.source.directory` field to an Argo CD Application resource when deploying plain manifests from a directory, specifically whether Argo CD will fail to automatically detect plain manifests if this field is omitted.

In Argo CD, if `spec.source.path` is specified and `spec.source.chart` is not, Argo CD looks at the specified path in the repository.
If `spec.source.directory` (or specifically `spec.source.directory.recurse`) is not set, Argo CD defaults to treating the directory as a Kustomize application if a `kustomization.yaml` is found, or Helm if a `Chart.yaml` is found.
If neither is found, Argo CD automatically defaults to treating it as a directory of plain YAML manifests (or JSON). It automatically detects plain manifests without needing `spec.source.directory` to be explicitly set.

Therefore, it is not necessary to explicitly add the `spec.source.directory` field for Argo CD to automatically detect plain manifest files. The statement is false.

Let me double-check:
Argo CD documentation states: "If no kustomization.yaml or Chart.yaml is found, Argo CD will automatically attempt to use plain YAML manifests."
So the field `spec.source.directory` is not strictly required for it to detect plain manifests. It defaults to directory.
Thus, the statement "If this field is not specified, Argo CD will not automatically detect that the source repository/path contains plain manifest files" is False.

I must provide ONLY the answer, expressed as a single letter, either T or F.

A: [33mf[0m
- Expected: [34mf[0m
  Match: f
- [32;1mPASS[0;22m

[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m However, at present, in our Argo CD Application, Argo CD is deploying files with types ".yaml", ".yml", and ".json". I only want Argo CD to deploy "*.yaml" files defined within that directory.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m What field can we set in the Argo CD Application resource, in order to tell Argo CD to only deploy "*.yaml" files?
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m Only specify the name of the field and the value of the field. For example: "spec.source.directory.(key): (value)". Include BOTH the key and the value.
[2;1m>[22;22m

Reasoning:
- The user wants to configure an Argo CD Application of type `directory` to only deploy `*.yaml` files, ignoring `*.yml` and `*.json` files.
They are asking for the specific field and value in the Argo CD Application manifest.

Looking at the Argo CD documentation for directory-type applications:
To filter files in a directory, you can use the `spec.source.directory.exclude` or `spec.source.directory.include` fields.

By default, Argo CD deploys all `.yaml`, `.yml`, and `.json` files.
If I want to *only* deploy `*.yaml` files, I can either:
1. Include only `*.yaml`: `spec.source.directory.include: "*.yaml"`
2. Exclude `*.yml` and `*.json`: `spec.source.directory.exclude: "{*.yml,*.json}"` (or similar)

The `include` field is a glob pattern to match files. If specified, only files matching the pattern are included.
The `exclude` field is a glob pattern to exclude files.

Since the goal is to "only deploy *.yaml files", `spec.source.directory.include: "*.yaml"` is the most direct and accurate answer.

Let's double check the exact field name.
In the Application spec:
```yaml
spec:
  source:
    directory:
      include: "*.yaml"
```
Or
```yaml
spec:
  source:
    directory:
      exclude: "*.json,*.yml"
```

The user's example format: "spec.source.directory.(key): (value)"

If I use `include`, the key is `include` and the value is `"*.yaml"`.
So: `spec.source.directory.include: "*.yaml"`

Are there any other considerations? Argo CD supports `recurse`, `exclude`, `include`.
If I set `spec.source.directory.include: "*.yaml"`, it will only include files ending in `.yaml`.

Let's review the exact string format requested.
"Only specify the name of the field and the value of the field. For example: "spec.source.directory.(key): (value)". Include BOTH the key and the value."

So the answer should be exactly:
spec.source.directory.include: "*.yaml"

I need to check the Argo CD documentation regarding Application Controller sharding methods.

Argo CD Application Controller supports sharding to distribute the processing of applications across multiple replicas.
The sharding methods supported in Argo CD are typically specified via the `ARGOCD_CONTROLLER_SHARDING_METHOD` environment variable or the `--sharding-method` parameter.

Looking up the Argo CD documentation for sharding methods:
The supported sharding methods are:
1. `legacy` - the default method used before, which uses a static hash ring.
2. `consistent-hashing` - uses a consistent hash ring, which minimizes resharding when replicas are added or removed.

Is `scalable-hashing` a supported method?
No, the supported methods are `legacy` and `consistent-hashing`.
Wait, let me double check. Maybe there's a newer method?
Let me search my knowledge base for "Argo CD sharding method scalable-hashing".
No, `consistent-hashing` was introduced to replace `legacy`. I don't recall `scalable-hashing` being a valid option.

Let's confirm the exact names.
In the Argo CD source code (e.g., `util/argo/argo.go` or `controller/sharding/sharding.go`), the `ShardingMethod` enum or constants usually define `legacy` and `consistent-hashing`.
Therefore, `scalable-hashing` is not a supported sharding method.

[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m Provide ONLY the answer. The answer is the name and value of the annotation to add. Dont quote the answer or use markdown.
[2;1m>[22;22m

    *   **Tool:** Argo CD
    *   **Problem:** Deploying a custom resource before its CustomResourceDefinition (CRD) is deployed, causing a dry-run error because the API server doesn't recognize the custom resource type yet.

Let's analyze the YAML:
```yaml
apiVersion: v1
kind: ConfigMap
metadata:
  name: argocd-cm
  namespace: argocd
data:
  url: https://argocd.example.com
  dex.config: |
    connectors:
      # GitHub example
      - type: github
        id: github
        name: GitHub
        config:
          clientID: aabbccddeeff00112233
          clientSecret: $dex.github.clientSecret
          orgs:
          - name: your-github-org
```

Checking the documentation for Argo CD SSO with Dex:
The `argocd-cm` ConfigMap uses `dex.config` to store the Dex configuration.
In the Dex configuration, the secret can be referenced as `$dex.github.clientSecret` (this references the `argocd-secret` ConfigMap/Secret, specifically the key `dex.github.clientSecret` in the `argocd-secret` Secret). Wait, actually, in `argocd-cm`, the format for referencing secrets from `argocd-secret` is `$<key>` where `<key>` is the key within the `argocd-secret` Kubernetes Secret. So `$dex.github.clientSecret` is correct.

Let's check the GitHub connector config for Dex:
```yaml
connectors:
- type: github
  id: github
  name: GitHub
  config:
    clientID: $GITHUB_CLIENT_ID
    clientSecret: $GITHUB_CLIENT_SECRET
    orgs:
    - name: your-github-org
```

Wait, what about `orgs`?
The GitHub connector config expects `orgs` as a list of objects, each with a `name` field.
```yaml
orgs:
- name: your-github-org
```
This is valid.

Let's verify the `$dex.github.clientSecret` syntax. Argo CD allows referencing secrets from the `argocd-secret` Secret using the `$<secret_key>` format. So `$dex.github.clientSecret` will look up the `dex.github.clientSecret` key in `argocd-secret`. This is explicitly documented in Argo CD docs for SSO:
"To reference a secret from the `argocd-secret` Kubernetes secret, use the format `$<secret_key>`."
So `$dex.github.clientSecret` is correct.

Are there any missing required fields or incorrect field names?
- `type: github`
- `id: github`
- `name: GitHub`
- `config:`
- `clientID: ...`
- `clientSecret: ...`
- `orgs:`
- `- name: ...`

This is exactly the standard Argo CD documentation example:
```yaml
  dex.config: |
    connectors:
      - type: github
        id: github
        name: GitHub
        config:
          clientID: aabbccddeeff00112233
          clientSecret: $dex.github.clientSecret
          orgs:
          - name: your-github-org
```

Therefore, the configuration is correct.

Let me double check if there are any subtle errors.
Is it `clientID` or `clientId`? Dex uses `clientID`.
Is `orgs` a list? Yes.
Is `name` the correct field inside `orgs`? Yes.
Does the top level key have to be `connectors`? Yes, Dex config `connectors` is a list.
Is `dex.config` the correct key in `argocd-cm`? Yes.
